InvalidRequestException(\"Invalid request, potential reasons: kafka client configured with the \" +\n                    \"wrong security protocol, it does not support KIP-43 or it is not a kafka Each user\n    41→ * is specified with user_<username> as key and <password> as value. This is consistent\n    42→ * with Zookeeper Digest-MD5 implementation.\n    43→ * <p>\n    44→ * To avoid storing clear passwords on disk or to integrate with external authentication\n    45→ * servers in production systems, this module can be replaced with a different implementation.\n    46→ *\n    47→ */\n    48→public class PlainSaslServer implements SaslServer {\n    49→\n    50→    public static final String PLAIN_MECHANISM = \"PLAIN\";\n    51→\n    52→    private final CallbackHandler callbackHandler;\n    53→    private boolean complete;\n    54→    private String authorizationId;\n    55→\n    56→    public PlainSaslServer(CallbackHandler callbackHandler) {\n    57→        this.callbackHandler = callbackHandler;\n    58→    }\n    59→\n    60→    /**\n    61→     * @throws SaslAuthenticationException if username/password combination is invalid or if the requested\n    62→     *         authorization id is not the same as username.\n    63→     * <p>\n    64→     * <b>Note:</b> This method may throw {@link SaslAuthenticationException} to provide custom error messages\n    65→     * to clients. But care should be taken to avoid including any information in the exception message that\n    66→     * should not be leaked to unauthenticated clients. It may be safer to throw {@link SaslException} in\n    67→     * some cases so that a standard error message is returned to clients.\n    68→     * </p>\n    69→     */\n    70→    @Override\n    71→    public byte[] evaluateResponse(byte[] responseBytes) throws SaslAuthenticationException {\n    72→        /*\n    73→         * Message format (from https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc4616):\n    74→         *\n    75→         * message   = [authzid] UTF8NUL authcid UTF8NUL passwd\n    76→         * authcid   = 1*SAFE ; MUST accept up to 255 octets\n    77→         * authzid   = 1*SAFE ; MUST accept = UTF1 / UTF2 / UTF3 / UTF4\n    82→         *                ;; any UTF-8 encoded Unicode character except NUL\n    83→         */\n    84→\n    85→        String response = new String(responseBytes, StandardCharsets.UTF_8);\n    86→        List<String> tokens = extractTokens(response);\n    87→        String authorizationIdFromClient = tokens.get(0);\n    88→        String username = tokens.get(1);\n    89→        String password = tokens.get(2);\n    90→\n    91→        if (username.isEmpty()) {\n    92→            throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: username not specified\");\n    93→        }\n    94→        if (password.isEmpty()) {\n    95→            throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: password not specified\");\n    96→        }\n    97→\n    98→        NameCallback nameCallback = new NameCallback(\"username\", username);\n    99→        PlainAuthenticateCallback authenticateCallback = new PlainAuthenticateCallback(password.toCharArray());\n   100→        try {\n   101→            callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{nameCallback, authenticateCallback});\n   102→        } catch (Throwable e) {\n   103→            throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: credentials for user could not be verified\", e);\n   104→        }\n   105→        if (!authenticateCallback.authenticated())\n   106→            throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Invalid username or password\");\n   107→        if (!authorizationIdFromClient.isEmpty() && !authorizationIdFromClient.equals(username))\n   108→            throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id that is different from username\");\n   109→\n   110→        this.authorizationId = username;\n   111→\n   112→        complete = true;\n   113→        return new byte[0];\n   114→    }\n   115→\n   116→    private List<String> extractTokens(String string) {\n   117→        List<String> tokens = new ArrayList<>();\n   118→        int startIndex = 0;\n   119→        for (int i = 0; i < 4; ++i) {\n   120→            int endIndex = string.indexOf(\"\\u0000\", startIndex);\n   121→            if (endIndex == -1) {\n   122→                tokens.add(string.substring(startIndex));\n   123→                break;\n   124→            }\n   125→            tokens.add(string.substring(startIndex, endIndex));\n   126→            startIndex = endIndex + 1;\n   127→        }\n   128→\n   129→        if (tokens.size() != 3)\n   130→            throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Invalid SASL/PLAIN response: expected 3 tokens, got \" +\n   131→                tokens.size());\n   132→\n   133→        return tokens;\n   134→    }\n   135→\n   136→    @Override\n   137→    public String getAuthorizationID() {\n   138→        if (!complete)\n   139→            throw new IllegalStateException(\"Authentication exchange has not completed\");\n   140→        return authorizationId;\n   141→    }\n   142→\n   143→    @Override\n   144→    public String getMechanismName() 166→\n   167→    @Override\n   168→    public byte[] wrap(byte[] outgoing, int offset, int len) {\n   169→        if (!complete)\n   170→            throw new IllegalStateException(\"Authentication authentication through a layered architecture. The core broker-side SASL authenticator is SaslServerAuthenticator (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java), which implements the Authenticator interface and manages the entire authentication flow on the broker side. It defines a SaslState enum to track authentication state transitions (INITIAL_REQUEST -> HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST -> HANDSHAKE_REQUEST -> AUTHENTICATE -> COMPLETE or FAILED). The authenticate() method is the main entry point that orchestrates the authentication process. Mechanism selection occurs in handleKafkaRequest() which parses incoming Kafka requests, and handleHandshakeRequest() which validates the client-requested mechanism against the broker's enabled mechanisms (configured in BrokerSecurityConfigs). When a supported mechanism is selected, createSaslServer() instantiates the appropriate SaslServer implementation based on the mechanism type. For GSSAPI, it uses special handling via createSaslKerberosServer() to create a Kerberos-authenticated subject. The broker supports four SASL mechanisms: PLAIN (PlainSaslServer in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java), SCRAM (ScramSaslServer in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java), GSSAPI/Kerberos (using Java's built-in mechanism with KerberosClientCallbackHandler), and OAUTHBEARER (OAuthBearerSaslServer in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java). Each mechanism has a corresponding SaslServer implementation, SaslServerProvider factory, and CallbackHandler. SCRAM mechanisms (SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512) are defined by ScramMechanism in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMechanism.java. The authentication context lifecycle is managed by SaslAuthenticationContext (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java), which encapsulates the SaslServer instance, security protocol, client address, and listener name. This context is created after successful mechanism negotiation and passed through the authentication pipeline. Token exchange occurs via evaluateResponse() on each mechanism's SaslServer implementation, with responses being sent back through the transport layer. After authentication succeeds, the SaslServer provides the authenticated principal through getAuthorizationID(), which DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java) uses to build a KafkaPrincipal. For GSSAPI, KerberosShortNamer is applied to transform the principal name. The SaslServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java) handles callbacks during authentication, dispatching to mechanism-specific handlers like PlainServerCallbackHandler and ScramServerCallbackHandler for credential validation. SaslExtensions allow per-mechanism extensions to the authentication protocol.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":258,"cache_read_input_tokens":58145,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":258},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"6d742bb9-f4c9-449d-a90f-acb2595a6304","uuid":"32cf822d-eaea-4e8c-bcc9-2d01efd80614"}
